The Labor Unrest at the International Settlement Telephone Company is Becoming Serious 120

Police Strictly Prevent Workers from Sabotage

Workers Hold Another Congress of Representatives

The strike by workers at the International Settlement Telephone Company has become increasingly serious since the breakdown of negotiations. The police are also very strict in their prevention measures. The strike committee held a congress of representatives yesterday, and worker leader Yao Yuesheng was beaten again. Although the automatic telephone exchange is still operating normally, the sound is low and turbid. The various situations are recorded separately below.

Increased Prevention Since the breakdown of negotiations, the Public Concession police, at the request of the company, fearing that the striking workers would sabotage the automatic telephone exchange, have increased the number of Chinese and Western armed detectives stationed at the entrances of the Central Bank on Jiangxi Road, the New Central Bank on Fujian Road, the North Branch on Haining Road, the Branch on Metherst Road, the South French Branch on Bisson Road, the New South French Branch on Minte Nyong Road, the East Branch on Jushan Road, the Road Sheng Branch on Yidingpan Road, and the Yangshupu Repair Shop. Prevention has been increased, and strangers are prohibited from entering and leaving. Senior Chinese staff members of the company are also interrogated.

Forced Communication The company has completely rejected the conditions put forward by the strike committee and does not recognize the strike committee. It only allows the workers to return to work unconditionally and asks the police to protect them to prevent the workers from stopping the communication. However, because the strike has lasted for nine days and the weather is humid, the workers in the automatic exchange test lines, motor room, ground lines, (blank) lines, air ducts, and aerial lines have mostly joined the strike. For example, when the workers change shifts at 8:00 AM, 5:00 PM, and 12:00 midnight, they must test the automatic exchange for damage. It is now necessary to reduce the number of tests, so the sound of the communication is not very clear and is slow. However, the company is trying its best to restore the situation.

Worker Leader Beaten Yesterday morning, Yao Yuesheng, the Chinese worker leader of the new installation room on Fujian Road, informed the workers in the new installation room that the company had accepted the basic conditions put forward by the strike committee and hoped that they would return to work at the company as soon as possible. As a result, more than 200 workers went to the company together at 10:00 AM to prepare to return to work. Later, they did not see the worker leader. When they asked engineer Wilson, they learned that it was not true. At 11:00 AM, they all withdrew and met the worker leader near Qingliange on Hubei Road. They questioned him and beat him, but fortunately he was not injured.

Attitude of Worker Leaders A reporter from the New Voice Society asked the worker leaders about their attitude towards the strike yesterday at No. 113 Yuan Shu, according to them, all the workers are on strike because they cannot bear the oppression of the imperialist capitalists. The worker leaders are in the same position and should act in unison and never break the strike discipline. They have no prejudice against the strike committee and are very sincere in cooperating and fighting against the capitalists. The strike committee's actions towards the worker leaders this time are a misunderstanding.

Congress of Representatives The Jiangxi Road head office and various branches held separate meetings the day before yesterday and elected new representatives to participate in the work of the strike committee. Yesterday morning, they reported to the Tongshang Hotel. The strike committee held a congress of all representatives at 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon to discuss ways to deal with the company. It is heard that (1) they will insist on continuing the strike to seek the final victory; (2) each district and team will start a fundraising team to raise strike funds from all walks of life; (3) those who violate the strike discipline will be handed over to the strike court for trial.

Increased Telephone Prices in the Concession 121

Business Increase of 34.6 Percent

Other Increase of 25 Percent

Effective March 27 of This Year

The Public Concession Bureau's Information Office released a message stating that at the Board of Directors meeting on Wednesday of this week, the board had approved the Telephone Company's request to increase telephone prices in accordance with Article 13 of the Company's Concession Contract. The issue of increasing telephone prices had been submitted to the Public Utilities Committee for discussion. As a result, the committee recommended that the company's request be granted to increase prices according to the numbers in Mr. Ansey's report, and that items not explicitly mentioned in the report be increased accordingly, starting from March 27, 1932. At that time, the General Manager of the Concession Bureau also submitted a brief note to the committee, stating the results of the discussion between representatives of the two Concession Bureaus and representatives of the Company.

Due to the drop in the price of silver, the Company's capital expenditures have increased by 14 percent compared to the original estimate of Mr. Ansey. Moreover, there are significant shortcomings in Mr. Ansey's report. If implemented literally, the Company will lose the benefit of the allowed price increase. Mr. Ansey did not mention each item in the telephone price list. If items not mentioned are still charged at the original rate, there will be many loopholes, and the price increase can be evaded a lot. Therefore, the representatives of the Concession Bureau believe that the best way seems to be to correct Mr. Ansey's numbers so that they can be implemented, starting from March 27. At the same time, the request for a further increase in price will be investigated, and if reasonable, it will be implemented on a mutually agreed date in the future.

According to the opinion of the Chief Financial Officer, Mr. Ansey's suggestion is to increase the price of business telephones by 34.6 percent and other telephones by 25 percent. The company's position is that items not explicitly specified should not remain the same. He believes this is fair, so the price list currently proposed by the company has included items not explicitly mentioned according to Mr. Ansey's proportions, but there are still some installation fees and other expenses that have not been added. However, the fee for temporary installation exceeds Mr. Ansey's proportion, because the fee for temporary use is intended to be higher than that for regular use. Therefore, the Chief Financial Officer believes that the table proposed by the company is in line with the wording or spirit of Mr. Ansey's report and recommends that the Board of Directors approve it.

The General Manager then stated that what the Concession Bureau approves at this time is only the price increase request based on Mr. Ansey's price rates. If a further price increase is requested in the future, the company should submit detailed explanations to the two Concession Bureaus. The Deputy Chief Financial Officer stated that he had received a report from the representative of the French Concession that the representative was also preparing to recommend to the French Concession Bureau the adoption of the price list proposed by the company.

A member of the Public Utilities Committee asked whether the adoption of Mr. Ansey's price list should be retroactive to March 27. The Chairman of the Committee replied that, according to the Concession Contract, the Concession Bureau could not but allow this. Another member stated that, in order to avoid misunderstandings among users, the approved revised price list should be made public, and it should be clearly announced that any further price increases will not be allowed until the two Concession Bureaus have fully considered the company's detailed explanations. The members of the committee all expressed their agreement.

Li Jingzong Resigns as Aviation Director 122

German Side Tries Hard to Retain Him but Fails The Eurasia Aviation Company held its 12th Board of Directors meeting at its company on Renji Road yesterday. The Chinese directors present were Wei Yifu, Wang Zhiyuan, Li Jingzong, Lin Shi, Huang Naishu, and Wu Xixuan. The German directors were Schmidt, Borussen, and Fokker. The first item discussed was the company's organizational law. The Chinese directors felt that operating in accordance with the contract provisions was very inconvenient for personnel and other matters, and advocated that the authority of the General Manager should be effectively increased in the organization. The German directors, fearing that the Chinese side would abuse their power and hinder the German side's interests, advocated that the provisions of the contract should still be followed. The two sides' opinions were not compatible. As a result, it was decided by the general meeting to first promote Wei Yifu and Schmidt to study the organizational law drafted by the former General Manager Shuang Qing and Li Jingzong, and then submit it to the next Board of Directors meeting for discussion. Next, Wei Yifu reported that he had received a notice from the Ministry of Communications, a Chinese shareholder, that it was proposed to select Liao Guanxuan to fill the position of Director of the Operations Group, and that the original Director of the Operations Group, Li Jingzong, would serve as a Director. He asked the audience to decide whether this was acceptable. However, all the German directors expressed their opposition. The reason was that the Eurasia Aviation Mail Transport Contract was negotiated by Li with the German Hansa Aviation Company after a long period of consultation, and the Eurasia Aviation Company was also created by Li's painstaking efforts. Not only did he plan and preside over all internal facilities, but he also personally handled the adventurous test flights of new routes and negotiations with the authorities along the routes. If the Chinese side could not provide sufficient reasons to dismiss this most important and useful staff member, the German side, in order to take into account the future development of the company, would never agree to such a dismissal, even though it was in the minority in terms of voting. Li stated that although the German side's expression was intended to consider the future of the company, he felt very grateful for the excessive praise. However, since he had already decided to resign, he hoped that the issue of his stay or departure would not cause any embarrassment to both sides. At the same time, he immediately left the meeting to express his determination. Li's resignation telegram is excerpted as follows: To the Minister and Vice Minister of Communications, I, Li Jingzong, have worked tirelessly and sought progress since the establishment of the Eurasia Aviation Company and the operation of the Northwest Air Route. The current environment is deteriorating and I am afraid of failure. In addition to resigning from the position of Director of the company, I respectfully request that you approve my dismissal from all concurrent positions. Li Jingzong kowtows, etc. It is heard that Li holds important positions in the Ministry of Communications, including the head of the Aviation Section and a member of the Regulations Committee and the Material Procurement Review Committee.

Compensation for Losses at Wusong Machinery Factory 123

Our Side's Statement Comes First

Japanese Side Still Tries to Shirk Responsibility

Negotiation by China-British Company

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration yesterday sent a letter to the Takeover Committee stating that negotiations for compensation for the Wusong Machinery Factory, which was destroyed by the Japanese army, must still be conducted. On the one hand, the Central Bank of China negotiated with the Japanese side. The details are recorded below.

Retaining Compensation The Wusong Machinery Factory was occupied by the Japanese army after the January 28 Incident. At that time, internal machines, motors, and other items all fell into the hands of the Japanese because our railway bureau personnel did not have time to transport them out in advance. Although the takeover was carried out later, our railway bureau personnel, seeing that many items in the factory were lost, declared to the Japanese representative, Mr. Tokizawa Naoyoshi, at the time of the takeover that many items were missing and could not be received temporarily. The Japanese side resolutely refused. At that time, our side was under strong power and temporarily endured the takeover and signed a succession document. The document stated that all occupied items had been succeeded to the Chinese side. At that time, our side still retained the right to claim compensation for the missing items in the factory, and the representatives of the China-British Bank and the head of the Works Bureau, who were present, could testify.

Japanese Side Shirks Responsibility Recently, Japanese representative Okazaki declared to the Joint Committee that, regarding the Wusong Machinery Factory, because the Japanese side had signed a succession document with the Chinese side when handing over the factory, stating that all items had been handed over to the Chinese side, the Wusong Machinery Factory issue had nothing to do with the Japanese side thereafter.

Letter from the Two Railway Bureaus The Joint Committee subsequently informed our Takeover Committee of this point. The Takeover Committee immediately sent a letter to the two Railway Bureaus to inquire about the truth of the matter and what the situation was. The Railway Bureau replied to the Takeover Committee yesterday, stating that although the succession document was signed at the time, it still retained the right to claim compensation for the loss of all items in the factory, and the Japanese side should not shirk its responsibility.

Negotiation by China-British Bank The China-British Bank is negotiating with the Japanese side for compensation because the Japanese army occupied the Wusong Machinery Factory and damaged many items during the war. The Bank is also negotiating with the Japanese side due to the loan relationship. The Railway Bureau is also starting to investigate the losses of the Wusong Machinery Factory in detail in preparation for negotiations.

To Prevent Epidemics, Clean Drinking Water is Needed 125

Dr. Wu Liande's Talk

Hopes Health Authorities Will Pay Attention

The Mainland News reports that Dr. Wu Liande, Director of the National Seaport Quarantine Office, told the Mainland News yesterday (15th) that improving the habit of dumping garbage into the Huangpu River is only the beginning of our health and epidemic prevention campaign. The tiger epidemic this year is far from comparable to previous years. We must find a way to provide clean drinking water to the poor who cannot afford the current tap water prices, otherwise the consequences will be unimaginable. Today, the municipal authorities have not made appropriate provisions for supplying clean drinking water to hundreds of thousands of poor people in Shanghai, which is a major cause of the spread of the tiger epidemic. The water fees of the tap water companies are very high in the eyes of the poor and unbearable. I still remember that a year ago, the Public Works Bureau spent a lot of money to hire Mr. Hill, a New York expert, to come to Shanghai to investigate tap water. Mr. Hill's report advocated that lower water fees should be charged to the poor in this port, and the cost could be compensated by those who could afford it. Unfortunately, it was completely ignored and not implemented. It is hoped that the health authorities will discuss the issue of epidemic prevention this morning and also consider the issue of drinking water supply.

Public Opposition to Opium Monopoly 126

Business Circles: The Shanghai Municipal Citizens' Association, 16th District Branch, telegraphed the National Government yesterday, saying: "The opium monopoly is about to become a reality. All our merchants and people are deeply shocked. The lessons of the past are still vivid; who is without conscience? We strongly urge your government to issue a clear order to dispel rumors and to sweep away this harmful policy with swift and decisive action, for the sake of the nation's longevity." A declaration by the Shanghai West District Business Associations stated: "Since last year, the government, mindful of public opinion, voluntarily canceled the opium monopoly, hoping that the black scourge would not spread and that the shame of being called a 'sick man' would be washed away. Unexpectedly, rumors have recently spread that the government is considering reviving the old dream of an opium monopoly. We believe that since the central government has abolished this harmful policy before, it would not break its promise and lose the trust of the people. Moreover, the officials in power are all followers of Sun Yat-sen and would not dare to recklessly violate his teachings and adopt a suicidal policy. Therefore, we do not believe the rumors. However, the public discussion is becoming increasingly intense and seems to be true. Chinese and foreign newspapers in Shanghai have even reported that Wang Jingwei's recent visit to Shanghai was to persuade Song Ziwen to agree to implement the opium monopoly as a condition for Song's reinstatement. Although the authorities have not acknowledged this, the rumors suggest that there may be some truth to it. Opium is a powerful tool for destroying a nation. Even though many powerful governments are suffering from budget deficits, few have resorted to collecting taxes on opium. Are international financiers less intelligent than our country? Alas, the value of a government lies in its ability to seek happiness for its people. If the government cannot be maintained without implementing the opium monopoly, then what is the value of this institution that poisons our people? We are determined to eradicate opium and are willing to die for it. We pledge to lead the 500,000 merchants and people in this district in a desperate battle against the demons of drug trafficking. We hope that all compatriots across the country will rise up together to reverse the decline. We are overwhelmed with sorrow and do not know what to say." Shanghai West District Business Associations.

Women's Circles: The Shanghai Women's Suffrage Association, deeply concerned about the recent news of the opium monopoly, telegraphed the Executive Yuan yesterday, urgently stating: "To the Nanjing National Government: We have read reports and telegrams from various groups protesting the opium monopoly. We understand that the central government has decided to implement the opium monopoly system, causing widespread anxiety. The unacceptability of the opium monopoly is evident in the public opinion and discussions of recent years. Even the central government's anti-smoking authorities are hesitant and uncertain about this matter, wanting to implement it but not daring to, wanting to abandon it but not willing to. We believe they are also troubled and know that adopting this system is an act of betrayal of the country and the people. They are willing to sacrifice everything for temporary gains, neglecting the long-term harm. The central government is facing a financial crisis, which the people understand. However, besides opium, are there no other ways to solve the problem? Reduce the number of useless troops, cut down on redundant officials who waste public funds, develop legitimate sources of revenue, and reduce unnecessary government spending. There are many ways to increase revenue and reduce expenditure. If all these methods are deemed unfeasible and the opium monopoly must be implemented, indulging in power and using high-handed measures, then the central government's heart is set on profit and its hatred is for the people. It wants to exterminate the remnants of those who have suffered from man-made disasters, natural disasters, internal troubles, and foreign aggression. What have the people done to deserve such treatment? If they are forced to die, wouldn't they fight like cornered beasts, striving for their last chance of survival? We urge your government to carefully consider the situation, discern the advantages and disadvantages, and implement a complete ban on opium to appease the angry public and prevent sudden unrest. We await your decision with bated breath." Shanghai Women's Suffrage Association, printed.

Triangle Love Murder of Husband Case 131

The Murder Case on Yanping Road Solved

Cowardly Husband, Fierce Wife, Vicious Lover

Two Nephews Accuse for Uncle's Revenge

The Criminals Have Been Taken to the Public Security Bureau

The situation of an unidentified man being assassinated on the open space of Yanping Road next to the Shenyuan Dog Racing Track in Western Shanghai on the morning of the 14th has been detailed in this newspaper. It is now learned that this case is a major case of triangle love murder of the husband. Now the details are recorded as follows:

The Deceased's Condition: The deceased's name is Tang Rongzhi, 38 years old, from Yancheng. He made a living pulling rickshaws. He was naturally cowardly and worked hard. He married a woman named Yuan, who is now 37 years old. Her appearance is vulgar and her nature is lewd and unusually fierce. They have been married for nine years, but the husband sees his wife as a tiger and is very afraid of her, so they have no children. The couple lives in the 172nd room of the 9th Workshop on Binlang Road in Western Shanghai. Tang has two nephews, one named Tang Yuanjia and one named Tang Yuanli, who live in Zhabei and work in factories. Triangle Love: Yuan's nature is inherently lewd. One husband is not enough to satisfy her desire. Six years ago, she had an affair with a fellow villager named Gu Jide. At first, they secretly had an affair, and then they lived together at home. Tang was afraid of his wife as a tiger and dared not say a word. Yuan abandoned the old and loved the new, seeing her husband as a thorn in her side. Over the years, every time Tang returned home from work, he had to cook. Although the three of them ate at the same table, they treated Tang like a stranger. Gu also pulled a rickshaw. Recently, he and Tang rented a rickshaw together, taking turns to work. However, Yuan finally felt that her husband was an obstacle and scolded him all day long. The neighbors who heard it were all indignant. Even the two nephews were upset for their uncle, but they could do nothing.

Suspicion Solves the Case: After Yuan murdered her husband, she went to her nephews' place, saying that her husband had been out for two days and had not returned home, and she pretended to be alarmed. Her two nephews were suspicious. They all said that the assassination case was published in today's newspaper. They immediately went to the police station to ask to see the photo, which turned out to be their uncle Tang Rongzhi. They went to inquire near her house for a week and learned that she had indeed conspired with her lover to murder her husband. Yesterday morning, they took the woman and her lover Gu Jide to the Putuo Road Police Station to sue them. After the police chief briefly interrogated them, because the case occurred in the Chinese area, he ordered the deputy police chief to send Detective Shen Dehui to the 6th District Police Station for investigation.

Separate Interrogation: After questioning by District Chief Zhang, Tang Yuanjia, 31 years old, from Yancheng, resident of 38 Pushan Road, Zhabei, testified that he was a worker. Tang Yuanli, 25 years old, also from the same residence, accused Yuan and her lover of conspiring to murder Tang Rongzhi. Yuan, 37 years old, from Yancheng, resident of 172 Binlang Road, testified. Gu Jide, 34 years old, from Yancheng, who makes a living pulling rickshaws, stammered and evaded the murder of the deceased. After District Chief Zhang obtained the testimony, he considered the case to be a major one involving the accusation of murdering her husband, and ordered that the case be prepared and transferred to the General Bureau for investigation.

Wealthy Merchant Guo Ruman Deceives Female Painter into Marriage 132

First Wife Files a Lawsuit for Bigamy

Female Painter Also Makes a Scene

Guo Ruman, the son of wealthy merchant Guo Yonglan, is over forty years old. His original wife, Han Yueling, whom he married in the first year of the Republic of China, has three daughters, the eldest two of whom are already married, while the youngest is still at home. However, the love between Guo and Han has faded over the years. Guo became involved with other women and began to look for another. He heard that there were two female painters, the Xu sisters, in the City God Temple, who were both beautiful and talented. The older sister, Zhiqing, was nearly twenty years old and still unmarried. Guo asked Lian Jimin and Xing Chunhua to act as matchmakers, falsely claiming that he had never been married. The woman's uncle, Xu Guanchen, agreed to the marriage. They chose May 29th as the auspicious day and held the wedding at the Foreign Cloth Guild in Songjia Lane. The next day, Guo's first wife, Han Yueling, read an advertisement in the newspaper about her husband marrying Xu Zhiqing and was shocked. She immediately confronted her husband, hoping for a satisfactory resolution. As a result, she hired lawyer Yang Lizhi to file a criminal self-accusation with the First Special District Court against her husband Guo Ruman, the new bride Xu Zhiqing, Xu's uncle Xu Guanchen, and the matchmakers Lian Jimin and Xing Chunhua, requesting that they be punished according to the law. The complaint stated that they were guilty of bigamy and knowingly marrying a married person. The complaint stated that the plaintiff married the first defendant in March of the first year of the Republic of China, with the plaintiff's father Han Fangzhou and mother Han Ni serving as the officiants, and the defendant's father Guo Yonglan serving as the officiant, and Yan Shanshan and Han Bingwen as matchmakers. The formal marriage took place twenty years ago, and the plaintiff has since given birth to three daughters. The eldest daughter, Peizhen, is nineteen years old and married to the Fei family. The second daughter, Peiyu, is seventeen years old and engaged to the Zhou family. The third daughter, Peilin, is fifteen years old and still unmarried. The plaintiff was well-versed in family education. Since the marriage, she has only known how to follow her husband. However, the first defendant, Guo Ruman, was devoted to pleasure and did not work. Recently, he has become even more extravagant. On May 29th of this year, he held a formal wedding with the second defendant Xu Zhiqing in the hall of the Foreign Cloth Guild in Songjia Lane, Beijing Road, with Lian Jimin and Xing Chunhua acting as matchmakers. There is an announcement published by Guo Yonglan and Xu Guanchen in the newspaper on May 29th of this year as proof. The next day, there was another announcement in the newspaper thanking the guests. On the same day, there was also an announcement published by Guo Yonglan stating that he had not heard of the matters published in the announcement by Guo Yonglan and Xu Guanchen yesterday and could not be responsible. Therefore, the defendant Guo Ruman is already married and is guilty of bigamy. The evidence is irrefutable. Xu Zhiqing knowingly married him. The defendants Xu Guanchen, Lian Jimin, and Xing Chunhua helped the principal offender to commit the crime and deserve punishment. Therefore, in accordance with Article 5 of the New Agreement of the Public Concession Court, which states that other cases may be brought by the parties concerned, a self-accusation is brought requesting arrest and punishment in accordance with Article 254 of the Criminal Law. After the self-accusation was filed, the new bride Xu Zhiqing realized that she had been deceived. She had a conflict with the groom and returned to Ning alone in anger. It is heard that the court will soon summon both parties for a public trial.

News from the Postal Economic System Research Association 135

Will Recommend Specialized Personnel for Research. The Postal Economic System Research Association, with Wu Tiecheng and twelve other committee members, has not yet formally met since being appointed by the Executive Yuan, but the committee members have exchanged views and discussed methods several times. They all believe that the research on the fundamental improvements of the postal system's economy and system should be conducted by those with specialized postal knowledge or those with extensive experience in the postal field. Only then can perfect improvements be achieved. Each committee member has received a notice from Chairman Wu, stating that the first plenary meeting of the committee members will be held on the 18th at the Municipal Government. At that time, it is planned to propose that experienced postal specialists be appointed as commissioners of the research association to discuss and study the matter in order to facilitate the progress.

Opinions of the Postal Society: The Chinese Postal Society believes that the Postal Economic System Research Committee convened by the Executive Yuan is about to meet in Shanghai. Therefore, it has published a lengthy paper from the perspectives of theory and facts. The original text is tens of thousands of words long and is divided into three sections: (1) on savings and remittance business; (2) on airmail transportation; and (3) on allocations to the Ministry of Communications. Each section is further divided into several items. First, the principles of economics and finance are described. Second, the established rules of various countries are described. Third, the handling situation in our country is described. Finally, concrete solutions are proposed. To summarize its main points, regarding the Savings and Remittance Bureau, it is advocated to implement a merger. After the merger, the personnel should be screened and retained, and the accounts should be separated for postal and savings accounting. Regarding aviation, in principle, the post office should not bear subsidy obligations. However, in order to take into account the facts, the necessity of the routes should be reviewed, and a certain limit should be added to those that need subsidies, so as to facilitate postal services and not hinder the development of the postal service. Regarding the allocation of funds to the Ministry of Communications, it should be stopped immediately, and a special postal accounting system should be implemented. The surplus should be used to develop inland postal services and restore postal services in Mongolia, Tibet, and the border areas. However, before the Ministry of Communications' administrative expenses are resolved, the post office should temporarily remit a considerable amount each month to maintain it. In addition, no further orders should be issued for withdrawals. According to the society, it is organized by current and former postal personnel, and its purpose is to promote in-depth research on postal knowledge. Last time, it published lengthy articles on the issue of postage increases and the issue of postal rights in the Northeast, which attracted a lot of social attention. If any sectors have any opinions on the current postal economic issues and want to discuss them with the society, they can write to Shanghai Postal Box No. 336.

Fresh Meat Industry in Disaster Areas Appeals for Exemption from Donations 138

The Shanghai War Zone Industry and Commerce Revitalization Committee is vigorously carrying out the war zone revitalization plan and plans to request the authorities to exempt war zone donations and taxes. The committee received yesterday a petition from the Shanghai Fresh Meat Industry Association, forwarded by Ye Shunxing and 24 other merchants in the disaster areas of Jiangwan, Wusong, and Zhenru, to the Shanghai Municipal Government, requesting that it be forwarded. The petition states that the petitioners, Guan Xiangsheng, Xian Baoshun, Shen Changfu, Zhang Jingchun, Gu Wenyu, Wang Peixi, and others, are fresh meat merchants from the disaster areas of Jiangwan, Wusong, and Zhenru. It is submitted to request a compassionate understanding of the severe suffering and difficulty in resuming business in the war zones, and to order a postponement of the collection until six months later, so as to ease the burden. The disaster victims' fresh meat shops in various places suffered severe damage from the invasion of the Japanese pirates on January 28th. After more than a month of fierce fighting and occupation, they were subjected to destruction and bombing, which was extremely intense. Houses were destroyed, families were broken, and lives were lost. It is now possible to gradually collect the refugees and return to their hometowns. The disaster victims were forced to build thatched sheds on the rubble and wilderness, hoping to reorganize their old business. However, they received notices from the Inspection Department of the Health Bureau and the Collection Department of the Finance Bureau, stating that they would continue to levy the post-slaughter inspection fee and slaughter tax according to the old point system. The suffering of the disaster victims after the disaster is still not relieved. Only a small number of disaster victims have scraped together money from all over the place, pawned their belongings, and borrowed money to beg the government for the slaughter improvement funds, and the charity relief funds released by the management committee. They used this to buy fresh pigs for slaughter and distribution, hoping to make a small profit to support their families. How can they talk about resuming business? How can they bear the burden of the officials coming to collect taxes? Under duress, they jointly signed and sealed this petition to appeal to the Mayor to show compassion and care, and to order Director Hu of the Health Bureau and Director Cai of the Finance Bureau to show kindness and empathy, and to allow the disaster areas to postpone the collection for six months, so that the survivors of the disaster can regain their breath.

###济生会执监联席会议

The Chinese Red Cross Society held a joint meeting of the supervisors and executive committee’s six groups yesterday. More than thirty people attended, including Chairman Wang Yiting, Vice Chairmen Xu Qianlin and Huang Hanzhi, and various committee members. A certain Director Zhenwu reported on the disaster relief efforts of the previous year in Anhui South, Anhui North, Jiangsu Jiangning Jurong, Jiangnan Jiangbei, Henan Nanyang Dengxian Tanghe Xinye Biyang, Shaanxi Wugong and other counties. The relief funds allocated by the provinces of Henan, Anhui, and Shaanxi were insufficient. The report listed relief funds, clothing, and other items from January 1st to May 31st of this year. As of the end of May this year, the funds already determined but not yet paid, after deducting deposits, showed an actual loss of tens of thousands of yuan (2). The Society was involved in disaster relief for both Shanghai and Jiangsu during the January 28th Japanese invasion of Shanghai, which caused heavy shelling. Four refugee camps were set up in Shanghai and one wounded soldier hospital, as well as seven refugee camps in Jiangsu. The expenditures for these are listed in a separate detailed account. According to the director’s report, the Society currently lacks tens of thousands of yuan. Due to the sluggish market, sources of funds have been exhausted. Furthermore, the work on the dikes and embankments in various counties in the provinces of Jiangsu, Anhui, Henan, and Jiangxi has not yet been completed. The people lack seeds and food, and starvation is widespread. Letters and telegrams requesting aid arrive like snowflakes. Although some aid is provided, it is a drop in the bucket and does not solve the problem. The greatest difficulty is the large number of displaced people in the Shanghai area, requiring substantial funds for relief. Although efforts are made to provide some assistance, it is very limited, causing deep regret among the staff. In the counties of Henan Nanyang Dengxian Xinye Biyang Tanghe, the disaster is severe, but the relief funds are meager, making the aid feel like no aid at all.

There is no solution to the issue. Additionally, the Haitang dike project in Ninghai, Zhejiang, still lacks more than ten thousand yuan, making assistance impossible. Neither abandoning it nor continuing it is acceptable. Due to continuous heavy rain, the project is in jeopardy and in a precarious state, causing great anxiety (3). The rescue team’s Director, Zhang Weixianqing, reported that the various accounts of the rescue team are listed in a separate statement. The Shanghai rescue team of the Society rescued tens of thousands of displaced people from January 29th to May 31st, including more than six hundred and forty wounded soldiers. The refugee camps accommodated over five thousand six hundred and fifty people, and more than three thousand one hundred people were provided with funds to return to their hometowns. All have now been assisted in their departure (4). Zhu Weiqichen said that in these times of natural and man-made disasters, with widespread suffering, these kinds of phenomena occur because people's hearts are not as they used to be, morality has declined, and thriftiness is not practiced. These three points will lead to the shaking of the foundation of the nation and the bankruptcy of the economy. Not only is this the case in our country, but also in many other European countries, where there is also no peace and tranquility. The crisis facing our country is becoming increasingly urgent and difficult to remedy. If society does not awaken again, the future is bleak. If we want to eliminate the calamities, we must first start by rectifying people's hearts. If we want to rectify people's hearts, we must promote morality, such as loyalty, filial piety, benevolence, love, trustworthiness, righteousness, and peace, with the promotion of thriftiness as the guiding principle. Our Society, as a charitable organization, should unite as many like-minded people as possible to advise and rescue people in the major matters of morality and thrift. Over time, there may be hope of transforming people's hearts and reversing the final calamity. Otherwise, if the water and drought disasters of recent years spread to sixteen provinces, and if the provinces that were affected by disasters last year experience another poor harvest this year in the late autumn rainy season, then the troubles facing our country will be unimaginable. I hope everyone will pay attention to this. All of us should encourage ourselves and others, widely promote these ideas, and announce them in newspapers so that everyone can be inspired to take action in order to reverse the situation. (5) Director Zhenwu and Zhang Weixianqing proposed that Zheng Chuheng, the chairman of the Liuhe branch, reported that due to the tragic disasters after the war in Liuhe Qianjing Yiqiao Yanglinkou Qiyakou Xintangshi and other places, there are five or six hundred households of disaster victims who have no homes to return to. They requested appropriate relief. After deliberation, it was decided to allocate two hundred and thirty shi of rice to be distributed by Zheng Chuheng, along with relief workers, specifically to the poorest households in Liuhe and other places. The funds must not be wasted, and the work must be practical. The public approved and resolved the matter. The meeting adjourned at six o'clock.

大塲災民之呼籲 145

Appeal of the Disaster Victims of Dachang

Objections to the Distribution of Relief Funds: Shen Feixiong, Yao Liting, Yu Hengfu, Lu Mingzhong, Lu Sheng, and other disaster victims of Dachang heard that the Jiangsu War Zone Relief Association had allocated 80,000 yuan for Baoshan relief and plans to distribute it by district within a few days, allocating it equally to the number of disaster-stricken households in the entire county. Various local groups believe that Dachang suffered the most damage and should not be allocated in this way. They are appealing to all parties, expressing their opposition. Their words roughly stated: This disaster, in addition to Shanghai, is the most severe in Baoshan Province. Among the counties of Baoshan, Dachang is the most affected. Miaohang Sanbai Mu and other places within the war zone are under the jurisdiction of Dachang, resulting in more than two thousand households being burned, bombed, or damaged by artillery fire in the nearby area. The severity of the disaster is self-evident. Other areas, such as Luodian and Liuhang, have not suffered direct losses and have no disaster to speak of. Relief should be based on factual needs. Now, the association is not using the severity of the disaster as the standard for allocating relief funds, but rather using the number of disaster-stricken households in the entire county as the standard. This not only contradicts the principles of relief, but also loses the effectiveness of relief. In order to seek real benefits, the disaster victims cannot remain silent. In addition to requesting the district chief to forward a request to the association to change the original proposal, they also ask people from all walks of life to uphold justice to comfort the disaster victims.

仁濟醫院昨開年會 146

Renji Hospital Held its Annual Meeting Yesterday

With Eighty-Five Years of History

Many Surprising Treatment Achievements

The Renji Hospital Donors' Annual Meeting was held yesterday afternoon at 5:00 PM at the new hospital site in the McTyeire Compound on Shandong Road. Sir Graham presided over the meeting and delivered a speech, stating that this annual meeting was the first at the new site and was worth commemorating. Seeing the tall buildings, completely new, was a far cry from the house on Pingzhi Road last year. He then described the changes Renji Hospital had undergone throughout its history and its service to the local community in great detail. Finally, Mr. Puff proposed and passed the 1931 report and financial statement. Mr. Puff then gave a thank-you speech on behalf of the Renji Hospital staff, which was answered by Dr. Patterson, the hospital director. Dr. Orr then stood up and reported on the aspirations of the Lister Medical Research Institute and the process of its establishment. Hui Jun then nominated Brown, Potter, Puff, and Wells as trustees, which was seconded and passed by Pan Zhiquan. Wells then nominated Bell, Brand, Zhang Lanping, Chen Bingqian, Chen Xuejia, Pan Zhiquan, Ni Xichun, Blythe, Wang Yiting, Hui, Huang Hanzhi, and others as hospital directors for 1932, which was seconded and passed by Mr. Chen. Finally, Dr. Patrick thanked the attendees on behalf of the chairman, and the meeting adjourned. Before the meeting, Dr. Chen Shaopu, the director of surgery, and others led the guests to visit the new hospital site. The location is spacious, and the buildings are tall and airy, with a total of six floors. All the equipment is perfect, and more attention is paid to surgery and first aid. For example, a special room is set up for the rapid rescue of opium poisoning victims, as there are suicides by poisoning in Shanghai every day. According to the hospital's report last year, a total of 1,155 people were sent for treatment for attempted suicide, including 521 women and 364 men who committed suicide by swallowing opium, totaling 885 people. Therefore, this equipment also meets the requirements of the local area. The X-ray department is located on the second floor and is managed by Dr. Payne. Last year, 1,860 patients were examined by X-ray, and 3,280 photos were taken. The operating room occupies a very important position in the hospital, with complete equipment. Last year, 1,422 surgical procedures were performed in the outpatient department, and 1,320 surgical procedures were performed on inpatients. According to Dr. Chen, the hospital performs major surgeries that are rarely seen elsewhere. A worker who had been suffering from abdominal pain for two years was admitted to the hospital for treatment. Dr. Chen performed surgery and removed about eight feet of his large intestine, and the disease was cured. Afterwards, the patient held the removed intestine and wrapped it around his abdomen, taking a photo for research. Such a case of removing one-third of the entire large and small intestines has only been recorded once in England. Recently, a patient named Lu Agao had a diseased gallbladder removed, which was as large as half a fist. An old man over sixty years old had a bladder disease treated by surgery and is still alive. Another patient named Jia had his entire anus and rectum removed and replaced with an artificial anus, and can still live normally. There are countless such cases. Finally, we visited the fifth floor, where the director of the research department is Dr. Orr. This department is named

the Lister Medical Research Institute, and also has a site on Aiwen Road, attached to Renji Hospital, which is part of it, to enable research and experimentation on patients. The work there is also quite busy. Last year's report, the 85th time, the McTyeire Compound Renji Hospital, from its inception in July 1846, to 1931, has gone through 85 years of history.

姚主敎路破獲嗎啡案審訊紀 157

Record of the Trial of the Morphine Case Cracked on Yao Zhujiao Road

Each Person Denies Any Involvement Cleanly: On the morning of the 12th of this month, Chinese and Western detectives from the Beidang Road Police Station in the French Concession cracked down on a private morphine manufacturing organization at a Western-style house at No. 121 Yao Zhujiao Road. They confiscated a large number of manufacturing machines and equipment, as well as finished and unfinished morphine raw materials in both dry and wet forms, weighing a total of more than 190 catties. Seven people from Sichuan, Zhao Youming and Ou Yongxiang, and their accomplices, Hou Yunshan and Hou Lihe, father and son from Guizhou, and Liu Mingzhang and Tu Hongfa from Sichuan, and Jin Yushan from Hubei were arrested and sent to the Second Special Court for prosecution and detention for investigation in accordance with Article 6 of the Anti-Smoking Law. The details have been reported in previous newspapers. Yesterday was the date for the continued trial. At 3:00 PM in the afternoon, Judge Xiong Hui and Clerk Gu Shouxi presided over the hearing in the First Criminal Court. First, the police lawyer Gu Shouxi stated that the investigation procedures on the police side had not yet been completed, and requested a postponement. However, for the benefit of the defendants, he requested that the trial be rescheduled for the shortest possible period. The court immediately ordered separate trials. According to Zhao Youming, he rented the house at No. 121 Yao Zhujiao Road in April, intending to move in himself in the summer. Later, Wang Hanzhang, a friend from Hankou, discussed with him that his family was coming to Shanghai and he did not have time to find a rental house. He asked me to sublet the house to him. Because we were friends for many years, I agreed, setting the monthly rent at 200 yuan and agreeing to start the lease on May 15th. He moved in ten days later. I transferred the hired Hou Yunshan, Hou Lihe, and Liu Mingzhang to Wang's employment. Wang went to Hankou after moving in to pick up his family in Shanghai. I knew nothing about the private manufacturing of morphine in the house. Hou Yunshan stated that he was hired by Mr. Zhao to guard the door at No. 121 Yao Zhujiao Road. I have only known Zhao for a month or so. I used to work for Director Qiu. When Qiu returned to Guizhou, he recommended me to Zhao for employment. Zhao sublet the house to someone else, and I did not know about it. But I only managed the downstairs, and never went to the second or third floors. I don't know about the morphine. My wages were paid by Zhao. Zhao came to check every two days, and no other outsiders came. Liu Mingzhang is the cook. However, there was someone who looked like a worker who came early and left late every day. I don't know what they were doing. Hou Lihe is my son. He washes the floor and serves tea. Jin Yushan stated that he was specially hired by Mr. Zhao to tend the garden and guard the door at No. 121 Yao Zhujiao Road, and to take care of a dog. I only went in for a week, and I don't know anything else. I don't know who rented the house. Usually, there were two or three people wearing short clothes coming and going empty-handed. I don't know what they were doing. Hou Lihe stated that he was hired by Mr. Zhao and had been there for a month or two. I didn't go upstairs. I don't know about the morphine. There were only five of us downstairs, including the five people in the case. I don't know about other people. Xu Hongfa stated that he only swept the floor and wiped the windows. He didn't go upstairs. He didn't know about the morphine manufacturing. I only went in for five days, so I don't know the details. Liu Mingzhang stated that he was the cook. There were seven people, including the five people here, plus two upstairs. The boss is Mr. Zhao, and I don't know the surname Ou. Ou Yongxiang stated that he did not rent the house at No. 121 Yao Zhujiao Road, nor had he been there. He knew nothing about the morphine. On the day of the arrest, I met Mr. Zhao on Sapo Sai Road. He told me to go to the police station with him. When I arrived at the police station, I was detained. I don't know why, etc. The defendants Zhao and Ou hired lawyers Xu Yannian and Zhao Zuwei for defense. The court ordered a postponement and another trial on the morning of the 20th of this month. The defendants were remanded to the police station.

周師英好行其德 158

Zhou Shiying Was Keen on Doing Good Deeds

Zhou Shiying, a Ningbo native who founded the Private Property Public Righteousness Association, established a nursing home in Nanxiang eight years ago. ###鳳陽輪買辦被髮妻控請離異

Once Mediated, No Compliance

Yesterday's Debate Concluded

Dai Xincai, from Yin County, works as a comprador on the Fenghuang Wheel steamboat. Recently, his wife, Zhao Cuiyun, also from their hometown, accused him of malicious abandonment and, through lawyer Zhou Bingyang, filed for divorce with the First Special District Court. The reasons stated are as follows: She married Dai five years ago, and they initially lived harmoniously. However, starting the year before last, he had an affair, became addicted to opium, and his behavior drastically changed. He frequently beat her, causing the plaintiff to suffer abuse and develop a desire to end her life. During the first month of the year before last, she attempted suicide by overdosing on tranquilizer water but was saved. When Zhao's brother questioned Dai, Dai acknowledged his wrongdoing and vowed to change. However, he was insincere. In June of last year, while home sick, he emptied all her dowry and refused to return her clothes and belongings. She had to temporarily reside with her mother, depending on her brother for support. In August and September, relatives were sent multiple times to persuade him to reconcile, but he refused. In October, as the weather turned cold and life became difficult, she sent a lawyer's letter warning him. She then received a reply from his lawyer, Song, advising Zhao not to harbor any other intention. Zhao had no other intention and, on November 5th, went to live with him. Unexpectedly, the defendant's parents and his younger brother, Xing Geng, tricked her out of the house, repeatedly refusing to let her return. She had no choice but to return to her parents' home. On December 1st, she again sent a lawyer's letter warning him. For half a year, there has been no news. Such behavior clearly indicates a complete severance of affection. Therefore, she filed a lawsuit requesting a divorce and asking the court to order him to pay alimony of three thousand yuan, as well as return her dowry and other items. This case has been heard, and the judge kindly advised them, hoping to reconcile them. He also verbally instructed Dai Xincai not to have any more affairs and to allow Zhao Cuiyun to use her dowry, and that his parents should no longer abuse Zhao Cuiyun. During the adjournment, both parties' lawyers were asked to mediate. However, during this adjournment, the two parties could not reach a satisfactory resolution. Yesterday, the court session was held again. The judge asked the plaintiff if she was willing to live with him, and the plaintiff replied that she wanted a divorce. The defendant claimed that after his wife left home, he had gone to pick her up several times, and his younger brother, Xing Geng, had also gone to welcome her back home, but the plaintiff firmly refused. As for the dowry and other items, they were still in the house. The plaintiff claimed that these were not facts at all, and presented to the court photos of Dai with his mistress as evidence. At this point, the court ordered the debate to begin and announced that the verdict would be delivered on the 22nd.

Letter

To the Editor: I am writing on behalf of my client, Xu Chen, who claims that the Shen Bao's local news column on the 14th of this month reported on the Caojing Defense Corps capturing a thief, stating that Xu Yongnian was killed and two bullet casings were found in his house. This is shocking. Xu Chen and her husband, Xu Yongnian, live in Sanjia Village and make a living by transporting manure. They are law-abiding, as everyone in the neighborhood knows. On the morning of the 12th of this month, Wu Rugui, the captain of the first squad of the Xiaomuqiao Defense Corps, and squad leader Zhu Maosong led more than twenty members of the corps to surround the thatched hut where she lived. They suddenly opened fire inside, firing more than a hundred shots. Her husband was fatally wounded and died. The captain and others then entered the house and conducted a thorough search, overturning beds and knocking down walls, but found nothing. They also threw her daughter, Mao Hai, from the bed to the ground, causing her death. My client's brother, husband, and daughter have suffered tragic deaths and are being unfairly accused. How can she remain silent? President Cheng Tianfang of Zhejiang University Temporarily Serves Concurrently as Dean of the College of Engineering after Resignation of the Original Dean 163

Funds Will Be Fully Disbursed Starting in July

Professors and Students Express Satisfaction

Hangzhou Correspondent: Li Ximou, Dean of the College of Engineering of Zhejiang University, resigned due to student dissatisfaction. President Cheng Tianfang returned to Zhejiang from Beijing the day before yesterday. This reporter visited the Zhejiang University Secretariat yesterday and learned that Dean Li resigned because of difficulties in managing the college and because he had accepted the Ministry of Education's invitation to go to Europe to investigate industrial education. He will be leaving soon, so he firmly requested to resign from the position of Dean of the College of Engineering. President Cheng had repeatedly tried to retain Dean Li, who had served in the position for a long time and was very familiar with the situation. Li was determined not to return to the college, explaining the various difficulties. Out of consideration for Dean Li, President Cheng did not want to force him to do something he found difficult. Li also proposed that President Cheng temporarily serve concurrently as Dean before a successor was appointed, to avoid the disruption of college affairs and the students' studies. After careful consideration, President Cheng also felt that this was the most appropriate solution during the transition period. Yesterday afternoon, he separately invited the professors and students of the College of Engineering to a meeting to announce this decision, asking the professors to continue teaching with peace of mind and to plan for the progress of the next academic year. He also reported on the results of his negotiations in Beijing regarding funding. President Wang and Minister Zhu were responsible for responding that the full amount would be disbursed monthly starting in July. Chairman Chiang was concerned about Zhejiang University and, in his personal capacity, telegraphed the provincial government to also fully disburse funds starting in July. With funding secured, the university's future is very promising. The professors and students all expressed satisfaction, so this matter has been completely resolved, which should be reassuring to those in society who care about the university.

Current State of Funding for National Central University 164

Since the resignation of former President Zhu, the National Central University has been facing a shortage of funds. Coupled with the national crisis, education throughout the country has been in a precarious state. In the past, the university was entirely supported by Jiangsu education funds, but since last winter, the Jiangsu Education Fund Management Office decided to cancel the funding, making the university's economic future even more bleak. Fortunately, the Ministry of Finance has taken on the responsibility. In early May, half of the salaries for April were issued. On the 21st, 60% of the salaries for November were issued. On the 4th of this month, half of the salaries for May were issued. On the 9th, half of the salaries for December were issued, with a gap of about one and a half months. (Location)

The notification and the instructions for attending the meeting are listed below:

Notification: Dear Sirs, At the previous general meeting of members of the Society (July 1930) and the national vocational education discussion meeting (August 1931), it was decided that the next meeting (i.e., this year's meeting) would be held in Liaoning or Fujian. Now, after the Northeast Incident, Liaoning Province has been lost and has not yet been recovered. In accordance with the previous resolution, the second location, Fujian, should be selected. It is now scheduled to hold the 12th general meeting of members and the 10th national vocational education discussion meeting in Fuzhou from August 8th to 10th, to report on the progress of the Society's affairs and to discuss issues related to vocational education facilities. All our comrades are urged to actively participate and jointly promote this grand event. It is greatly hoped that in the face of national crisis and the people's suffering, the need to promote vocational education is even more apparent for the sake of fundamental national salvation. The Fujian Provincial Education Authority is particularly enthusiastic in promoting vocational education, and its facilities are worthy of emulation. Holding the meeting there will not only increase interest but also ensure thorough discussions and achieve great results. In addition, Fujian Province has many beautiful landscapes for sightseeing after the meeting. Enclosed is a copy of the instructions for attending the meeting, which you are requested to examine and promptly respond to so that preparations can be made. Instructions for Attending the Meeting: 1. The meeting is tentatively scheduled to begin on August 8th. However, if the sailing schedule from Shanghai to Fujian requires adjustments of one or two days, a notice will be published in the newspaper at that time. 2. The Fujian Education Department has expressed its warm welcome to the meeting in Fuzhou and has telegraphed its agreement to send personnel to assist. The venue will be announced after it has been determined. 3. Attendance at the general meeting of members will be mainly for members of the Society. Each vocational education institution should, as in the past, designate one to three representatives to report to the Society in advance. 5. Members and representatives of various vocational education institutions who intend to attend the meeting must provide detailed information, including their name, railway or waterway stations of departure and arrival, and dates of travel and return, by June 30th at the latest. This information will be used to compile a roster to be submitted to the Ministry of Railways and the Ministry of Communications for approval. The Society will then send a certificate for discounted train or ship tickets, which can be used to purchase tickets from the various railway bureaus or the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company. 6. Members and representatives of vocational education institutions who have proposals should submit them to the Society by July 25th at the latest for compilation. 7. Except for members from Fujian and nearby areas who can go directly to Fuzhou from their point of departure, all others must bring simple bedding and luggage and first go to Shanghai, staying at the Xiangbin Hotel at the intersection of Simalu and Guangxi Road, to arrange for the transfer to Fujian (those who wish to stay at other hotels are welcome). 8. The name of the ship and the date of departure from Shanghai to Fujian will be announced in the newspaper at that time. 9. Other meeting-related information will be compiled into instructions for attending the meeting and provided upon arrival in Shanghai or after arrival in Fujian.

Random Notes from an Ancient Temple Bell (25) 167

"Do Not Remove the Garden Weeds," by Zhai Fu, 28

These few words written by Mr. Zhu have confused me. From my previous understanding, knowledge comes before action. But now Mr. Zhu considers action as the father, knowledge as the son, and creation as the grandson, which is exactly the opposite of my understanding. If I am right, then he must be wrong. If he is right, then I must be wrong. I think and think, and cannot say that I am definitely right, nor can I say that he is definitely wrong. I am going around in circles and cannot find a way out. Unable to justify myself, I finally asked Mr. Zhu for evidence to explain his argument.

Mr. Zhu asked me, "Do you know how to ride a cow?" I said, "Yes." "How did you acquire the knowledge of riding a cow?" "I learned it by riding on the cow's back a few times." "Good, riding a cow is action, and knowing how to ride is knowledge. So knowledge comes from action, doesn't it?" "Yes."

Mr. Zhu asked again, "Do you know how to swim?" I said, "Yes." "Think again about how you acquired the knowledge of swimming." "I learned it by swimming in the water a few times." "Good, swimming is action, and knowing how to swim is knowledge. So it can be seen that knowledge comes from action, doesn't it?" "Yes."

I thought for a moment and asked Mr. Zhu in return, "We know that fire is hot and we pull back our hands when we encounter fire. Knowing that fire burns is knowledge, and pulling back our hands when encountering fire is action. Isn't this knowing before acting?" Mr. Zhu said, "What is fire? What is burning? Did you know this from birth?" "I don't think I knew it from birth. Maybe someone told me." "Someone can tell you that fire is hot, and they can also tell you that fire is cold. Who is telling the truth, and who is lying? How do you judge, how do you distinguish, and how do you know? How do you know that fire is definitely hot and definitely not cold? How do you know that the person who told you fire is hot is telling the truth? And how do you know that the person who told you fire is cold is lying?" "I think I would try it with my hand on the fire and then I would know." "That's right. When you were in your mother's arms, you once reached out to play with fire and got burned, and then you knew that fire was a dangerous thing, so now when you see fire, you pull back your hand. Reaching out to play with fire is action, and knowing that fire burns is knowledge. Doesn't this prove that action comes before knowledge?"
