The World's Number One Swimming Wonder Woman 175

The Success Story of Miss Helen Madison (2) Huai Qing The Greatest Success

This Seattle girl, proficient in water sports, has the same speed and strength in long-distance swimming as in short-distance swimming. Her recent new record for 100 yards is 60 and four-fifths seconds, while her one-mile swim is 24 minutes, 34 and three-fifths seconds. The world records officially held by Miss Madison are as follows (all freestyle):

100 yards 60 and four-fifths seconds

100 meters 1 minute 8 seconds

150 yards 1 minute 40 and two-fifths seconds

200 meters 2 minutes 34 and three-fifths seconds

220 yards 2 minutes 35 seconds

300 yards 2 minutes 39 seconds

300 meters 3 minutes 59 and five-tenths seconds

400 meters 5 minutes 39 and three-fifths seconds

440 yards 5 minutes 39 and three-fifths seconds

500 yards 6 minutes 16 and two-fifths seconds

Half mile 11 minutes 41 and one-fifth seconds

One mile 24 minutes 34 and three-fifths seconds

In addition, the following four records are about to be officially recognized:

500 meters 7 minutes 12 seconds

1,000 yards 13 minutes 23 and four-fifths seconds

1,000 meters 15 minutes 44 and four-fifths seconds

1,500 meters 23 minutes 44 and three-fifths seconds

On August 14, 1931, she created her best one-mile record of 23 minutes, 34 and three-fifths seconds at the Washington Sports Association Swimming Pool in her hometown of Seattle, exceeding the highest record held by Nippon, but this achievement could not be officially recognized because it was not produced during a formal competition. The one-mile record was originally held by McKay, who started in the state of Oxiphu on August 30, 1925, and was defeated by Miss Madison. Helen's greatest success was breaking the 1,500-yard record in San Francisco on September 13, 1931. The record was originally set by Gale Gen in New York on August 12, 1988, at 24 minutes, 29 and one-fifth seconds, while Miss Helen shortened the old record by 196 and one-fifth seconds, with her time being 21 minutes and 13 seconds.

Like Mother, Like Daughter 176

Miss Helen has forgotten the circumstances of her first time learning to swim, but she still remembers the circumstances of her first time practicing "diving."

"I can always remember the circumstances of learning to dive," Helen said, "My mother encouraged, accompanied, and taught me to learn to swim, so that I could participate in swimming competitions and become a famous swimmer, to see my name in the swimming world in the Seattle newspapers, but I didn't want to learn at first, because I couldn't dive, my mother told me, "Diving is not difficult, as long as you jump correctly."

"At the time, there were many women who were very famous in the swimming world, but I couldn't measure how to move in the water, so I learned to dive when I was almost thirteen years old, and then I joined swimming competitions."

Mr. Tu De's Guidance 177

In 1927, Miss Madison participated in the swimming competition at the Seattle Youth Association Crystal Palace. Under the watchful eyes of the public, she finally won the championship in this swimming competition for about an hour. This was her first success, and she was praised as a young female swimmer, and it was also the success of her teacher Mr. Tu De's guidance. At this time, she was only a 14-year-old girl.

"Why don't you join our swimming team?" Mr. Tu De said to Helen like this, and Helen sympathized with his advice.

"When I first joined the swimming team, I was very scared, because everyone else was bigger than me and had better results than me," Helen thought to herself, "My results were very immature, but Mr. Tu De was very concerned about me. When the swimming preliminaries for the 1928 Olympic Games were held, all the blood vessels in my body were very tense, and I was very scared in my heart, because everyone was paying attention to such a young me, and I was also participating in the competition. Ah, I still can't understand why my immature results could attract people's attention. Mr. Tu De has been teaching me to swim since 1928, and he is the one who looks up to me the most.

Free Talk

Sayings of Old Man Ma Xiangbo at Ninety-Three

From Chickens, Cats, and Dogs to Resisting Hate Goods 178

— Lun Jiu

In large areas like Jiangsu and Zhejiang, it is said that there have recently been outbreaks of plague affecting chickens, dogs, and cats everywhere. Moreover, knife wounds and bloodstains have been found on these animals. The villagers are extremely frightened, and people say there are ghosts. Wherever the ghosts are, charms are used to ward them off, and wherever the charms fly, the plague spreads.

The plague among animals is associated with ghosts and charms, and from ghost drawings, I am reminded of a story from ancient Egypt. In ancient Egypt, there were many Jews, about five or six hundred thousand. The Egyptians became very afraid as the Jewish population increased day by day. Later, they devised various methods to mistreat them, and finally used secret and ruthless means to kill the firstborn sons of the Jews one by one, causing great alarm among the Jews living in Egypt. Fortunately, Moses emerged, and the Jews were saved.

Returning to the topic, if there really are ghosts who can draw charms, then Japanese goods are the charms. We are deluded by these charms, and the Japanese still want to kill us, causing families to be destroyed. This is entirely self-inflicted. However, knowing that these charms are the root of disaster, we still trust and believe in them. Where is our conscience? Especially those who traffic in hate goods, they only care about making money, knowing that these charm-like hate goods are enough to kill people, and they don't care. In my opinion, they are insane, and one day, the root of disaster will erupt, even more fiercely than the bomb in Hongkou Park.

I wonder, on the day when a bomb like the one in Hongkou Park is about to explode, where will these swaggering profiteers be?

Remembering Nie Zeng Jifen 179

— Hui

Many friends complain of poverty. When asked why, nineteen out of ten say it is due to the financial burden of their families. And the clothing and accessories of their wives and daughters account for most of it. A single pair of socks for the wife of an official costs twenty-five gold pieces, which could sustain a poor family of eight for a month. The country is in such chaos, and society is so unstable, yet many women are still indulging in a drunken stupor, competing with each other in clothing and accessories. If this continues, the nation will be doomed. Reading the "Thrift and Frugality to Save the Nation" essay, I feel that if every woman in China could be like Nie Zeng Jifen, there would be positive results after a few years. I can say this with certainty. Perhaps some readers do not know who Nie Zeng Jifen is. The reporter knows and is willing to introduce her. Nie Zeng Jifen is the second daughter of Zeng Guofan, a high-ranking official of the late Qing Dynasty. She was educated at home from a young age, learned to read, and was skilled in etiquette. Her son, Mr. Yuntai (the author of "Thrift and Frugality to Save the Nation"), was once quite famous. Now, he serves his mother with filial piety and believes in Buddhism, living quietly away from the world. The Nie family is a large and prominent one. Although Mrs. Nie is eighty years old and her family is not poor, she still wears simple clothes and eats plain food. In her spare time from managing household affairs, she holds family meetings every week to guide the family on what should be promoted and what should be changed. She also publishes the "Nie Family Sayings Monthly," which promotes thrift and encourages people to do good. In the cold season, she makes cotton clothes by hand to distribute to the poor. On Kunming Road, I once saw a dilapidated carriage, and it was Old Mrs. Nie going with her family to the nearby Guangzhong Dyeing and Weaving Factory to buy domestically produced cloth.

My Thoughts on Hen Shui 180

— Juan

Mr. Zhang Henshui has lived in Peiping (Beijing) for a long time. Although he is originally from Anhui, he has become somewhat Peiping-ized. Last year, he moved to Dapenglan, where the courtyard and garden are neat and beautiful, with many flowers and trees. Henshui writes diligently there, and although it is hard work, he finds much comfort in spirit. Therefore, his literary talent grows higher and his works become more numerous. Who knew that he would recently encounter a great misfortune? That terrible scarlet fever actually came to oppose his literary work, cruelly taking away his two precious daughters, causing him to no longer have the heart to engage in writing. And letters urging him to submit manuscripts are still flying in like snowflakes, forcing him to the point where he wants to stop but cannot. He has no choice but to pick up his pen and reluctantly make a living from the old papers. Alas, this is truly a small tragedy in life. I think of Henshui and cannot help but sigh for my own hard work.

After finishing "Tears and Laughter," Henshui once visited Shanghai. We often spent time together, with banquets every evening. After exchanging pleasantries, I deeply understood that he was upright and straightforward, with the spirit of a person from the Qilu region (Shandong). And what I most identified with him was his love for watching movies. In his spare time from writing, he would sit high in the movie theater, enjoying the various scenes on the screen. I once said to him, "After reading your 'Tears and Laughter,' I knew you loved watching movies. Because your depiction of the characters' actions is very detailed, just like the attention to small actions in good movies. You can be considered a Lubitsch of the novel world!" Henshui was humble, but also regarded it as knowing his heart.

Henshui stayed in Shanghai for about a month and often went to the Mingxing Film Company to discuss the filming of "Tears and Laughter." He gathered many photographs of famous Peiping scenic spots for the Mingxing colleagues to use as reference. He also explained in detail the personalities and identities of the characters in the book. Before leaving, he was especially serious and repeatedly entrusted Du He with the task of writing the screenplay. At that time, they originally wanted to shoot a silent film, but the Mingxing colleagues, for the sake of perfection, specially purchased sound equipment from Hollywood, USA, to go to Peiping for on-site filming. Henshui did his best to help, and was extremely busy. Everyone spent endless effort, and now it has finally been completed. I heard from Du He that this film not only has sound but also color, and all the explanations are entirely his work. When it is released, it will surely cause a sensation. Unfortunately, Henshui is far away in Peiping and cannot enjoy a sneak peek. I predict that he will be very happy to receive this exciting news. But thinking of his personal misfortune, he cannot help but feel depressed, perhaps like the characters in "Tears and Laughter," feeling a mixture of tears and laughter.

World News in Brief 181

— Hai Ke

The Menu in the British Royal Palace: For those fortunate enough to enter Buckingham Palace and attend the receptions of the King and Queen of England, most are so overwhelmed by being in the presence of royalty that they are afraid of making a mistake and cannot eat anything. This is especially true for young women who are attending the palace for the first time. They are particularly restrained. However, the Green Drawing Room still provides food and drinks as usual. If they suddenly feel hungry, they can freely enjoy the following menu:

Chicken à la Maréchale, Jellied Lamb à la Maréchale, Savory Mince Rolls, Assorted Sandwiches, Mutton Patties, Fresh Fruit Desserts, Fresh Bayberry Jelly, Assorted Cakes, Orange Soda, Lemonade

Among them, mutton patties seem too common to be included in the royal menu. However, the mutton patties in Buckingham Palace are made with special care. They are only about the size of a man's pocket watch, melt in your mouth, and are exceptionally delicious. They are not available except during grand banquets in the palace. As for those who are thirsty, there is also a special department that provides tea and coffee, as well as brandy and whiskey soda. But everyone is too afraid to drink too much.

Xinghua Longan in the Mouths of Foreigners 182

— Yan Yu

Standing atop the ancient and majestic city wall of Xinghua, we overlook the entire city, and what enters our eyes is like a large garden, so beautiful! This city in southern China is covered in a lush green color, with trees growing almost everywhere. Among these trees, most are longan trees, which Chinese people commonly call "dragon eye" trees. The cultivation of this fruit tree is a major source of wealth for the local people, and many people in Xinghua rely solely on this occupation to make a living. And the produced longan fruit is mostly sold in Shanghai.

In early summer, around May, visitors coming to Xinghua from elsewhere may vaguely recognize a few rare and exotic giant birds perched on many longan trees. But as soon as they run closer to the trees and look carefully, they will immediately discover that those climbing on the natural ladders formed by the branches are not really any giant birds, but gardeners carrying sickles.

In the eyes of others, their profession seems to carry a high degree of danger, especially in windy weather. However, the fact tells us that no one has ever heard the story of a gardener falling from a longan tree. These gardeners patiently bury themselves in their work on every branch, meticulously cutting down not only the dead branches, one by one

but also cutting off nearly half of the leaves and most of the flowers. Therefore, a pruned longan tree inevitably appears to have sparse leaves and scattered flowers. But without doing so, it is difficult to expect a full harvest in the autumn. In addition to pruning, considerable fertilizer is also required. It is necessary to apply manure about four times a year if you want the fruit to be of good quality.

In autumn, around August and September, the longans on the trees are all ripe. Clusters of brownish-yellow fruit hang on the branches, contrasting with the green leaves, so beautiful and lovely! Its taste is extremely delicious, with a special aroma that is exceptionally palatable, unmatched by any other fresh fruit. In the middle of the pulp is a black core, which Chinese people say looks like a dragon's eye, so they give this fruit another name, called "dragon eye." Although whether a dragon's eye really looks like this is still a question, it seems that no one dares to say for sure.

The wood of the longan tree is known for its hardness and durability, and the grain is smooth and delicate, very lovely. This wood is mostly used to make small tables, candle holders, or photo frames. The production of longan wood is extremely limited, because this tree grows very slowly, and its lifespan is particularly long. An ordinary longan tree can flower and bear fruit for about a hundred years. If it is specially cultivated, then it may be even longer.

Carefree Talk at the "Looking at the Echo" Studio 183

— Zhang Mingqi

Zhang Jianbai (Mingqi) became a Juren (successful candidate in the imperial examinations). In less than ten years, he rose to become the Governor-General of Liangguang (Guangdong and Guangxi). In the Qing Dynasty, the speed at which officials advanced was unparalleled. He was from Shandong. Initially, he was a tutor in the home of Yu Shouping (Chengge). He was dissolute and extravagant, and his clothes and belongings were all gone. His bedding was not washed for months. In the cold weather, he would sleep naked under the quilt. When guests came, he would talk eloquently. Every meal, the servants did not call him. Mingqi would enter the dining room himself. If he was late, he would not get food. He became accustomed to it. Chengge knew of this and wanted to humble him because of his arrogance. Mingqi also knew Chengge's intention, but he went his own way. The relationship between the host and guest was only outwardly harmonious. Eventually, he left. Through the introduction of his sister's husband, Xia Shuqing (Tongyi), he entered the staff of Cen Chunxuan. Chunxuan and Tongyi were classmates in the same year. They were close. Because of his affection for Tongyi, he also cared for Mingqi. He specially recommended him, saying that he had the talent to be of great use, claiming that he had the knowledge of Hu Linyi and the talent of Zuo Zongtang. He was specially granted the rank of Daotai and appointed as the Taiping-Sisun Daotai of Guangxi. At that time, Chunxuan was the Governor-General of Guangdong and Guangxi. Cen Chi, a member of his staff, was most heavily relied upon by Chunxuan. Chunxuan was going to appoint Mingqi as the Salt Commissioner of Guangdong and Guangxi and consulted with Chi. Chi said, "Jianbai's talent is certainly sufficient to successfully complete the task. But he does not enjoy fame and fortune. I am afraid it is not what he desires. Your Excellency, decide for yourself." The matter was dropped. Mingqi heard about it, thanked Chi for understanding him, and said, "My ambition is the same as yours. I do not like official advancement." Later, he was promoted to Guangdong Treasurer. After Mingqi took office, he once said to someone, "Governor Yun forced me to do it. I could not refuse." Shortly after, Lin Shaonian, the Governor of Guilin, was transferred elsewhere. Chunxuan strongly recommended Mingqi to succeed him. It happened that Chengge opened a government office in Guilin. Mingqi was arrogant and did not show him respect. A certain county had a vacancy, and Chengge appointed a certain magistrate. Mingqi did not think it was right. He hung a plaque on the front door, reprimanding the Provincial Treasurer for being incompetent. Historically, there was never a Governor who could reprimand a Provincial Treasurer with a plaque. It started with Mingqi. Chengge could not bear it and tried to leave. Mingqi's father, a certain person, once served as the Assistant Magistrate of Xiangtan County in Hunan. Chengge's father, a certain person, once served as the Patrol Inspector of Wuxue in Hubei. Both were over seventy years old in Guilin and were very close. They once agreed to climb Duxiu Peak hand in hand. The people of Guilin had a saying about it: "The fathers get along well, the elders are admirable. The sons do not get along, the high officials are too difficult." It was a laughingstock at the time. When Emperor Xuantong ascended the throne, Mingqi entered the court. Knowing that a certain Governor of Guangdong was not tolerated by the court, he bribed influential officials to take his position. He was only thirty-seven years old. When the country changed, he was driven out by the party members. Because he had been an official in Lingnan for a long time, he gained the friendship of Cen Chunxuan's former subordinates, Long Jiguang and Lu Rongting. He approached them with humble words and generous gifts. The two of them recommended him to the government. Those around Yuan Shikai told him, "This person is a member of Cen's party or someone close to Cen. It is better to be careful." Shikai laughed and said, "This person has a craving for wealth and status. He is not happy without wealth and status. If I give him high office and special powers, and he does not betray Cen and come over to me, you can gouge out my eyes." So he made him Governor of Guangxi and then transferred him to Guangdong. During the Bingchen campaign, Chunxuan resisted Shikai very fiercely. He sailed to Guangdong, persuading Jiguang and Mingqi to raise troops to march north. Jiguang agreed in word only. Mingqi refused in stern tones, and secretly reported to Shikai, saying that Chunxuan was plotting rebellion. Only then did Chunxuan realize that Mingqi would not be attached and had reversed his previous behavior, repaying kindness with resentment. He was furious and wrote a long letter breaking off relations, publishing it in the newspapers to show the world. From this, it can be seen that Chunxuan knew Mingqi, but he did not really know Mingqi. The one who knew Mingqi best was Shikai. However, both Mingqi and Jiguang were driven out. Hongxian (Yuan Shikai's short-lived empire) eventually collapsed, which Chunxuan accomplished with the help of Rongting's troops.

Record of Dual Life in the Military (81) 185

— Master of Seeking Happiness Studio

Chapter Ten: Powerful Officials and Ethical Collapse Bully Others; Fortunately, There are Women to Comfort Them; A Shortcut to Bribery and Advancement; Appointing Bandit Leaders to Command

"If you just come back and complain to me, so that you don't get sick from bottling things up, I am willing to listen to you. But please don't lose heart or be discouraged. Don't be too sad and damage your body and spirit. You need to know that I have tried my best to get you out and about, simply to seek a common future happiness for you and me. If hope hasn't been achieved at all, and I have only added a lot of trouble for you in vain, think about how I can be at ease seeing this from the side. What hope will there be in the future? Yutian, I beg you, think of it as you loving me. Be more open about everything, and don't be so sad anymore." Originally, doing things in the world is the most difficult thing. Now you and I are also born at the wrong time, encountering such a most

evil society. No matter what you do or which path you take, it is absolutely impossible not to suffer or endure hardship. The only way is to apply flexible tactics, hold a strong will, strive outward, and be philosophical inward, to tread the path to success through difficulties and dangers. You are certainly very wronged now, but if you compare yourself to me, I used to mix from childhood to adulthood in that dark and dirty place. The anger I suffered and the hardships I endured were probably thousands of times deeper than yours. And I wasn't even cared for or pitied like you are today. You are a man, and you can't bear just this? How did I, a weak woman, survive before?" As she spoke, she who was advising others not to be sad was also moved by grief, her eyes reddened, and her heart soured. She suddenly felt that the edges of her eyelashes were also a little wet. She quickly tried her best to hold back, and simply leaned her delicate body over, dodging away from his cheek. With a pair of slender hands, she held onto An Yutian's shoulders, slightly lowering her head and directly staring at An Yutian's face. Those watery autumn waves, half sobbing and half extremely frivolous, said in a coquettish voice, "I don't allow you... you have to look at me... look at my face... don't be sad or angry anymore... how about it?... won't you quickly smile at me?" As she spoke, she shook her hands repeatedly, shaking An Yutian like a clapper. After all, An Yutian didn't have a heart of iron or a body of steel. He couldn't help but laugh out loud with a "chī pū" sound. He kept begging for mercy, saying, "I won't anymore." Instantly, the gloomy atmosphere in the room was dispelled by a burst of laughter and vanished into thin air.

Slight Improvement in Yarn and Cotton Yarn Market 192

The cotton yarn market rose in the morning but weakened at noon due to the rebound in U.S. cotton prices. As the local market had already fallen for several days, a reaction occurred, improving sentiment. Some profit-takers took the opportunity to sell short, leading to a slight improvement in the market. However, the situation in the interior remains bleak, with people's livelihoods deteriorating, rampant banditry, and severe financial constraints, resulting in weak purchasing power. Consequently, some factories are facing difficulties with inventory. Therefore, the market situation recently has been weaker than the cotton market.

Strong Cotton Rebound 193

The cotton market trended firmer due to the rebound in U.S. cotton prices, and sentiment in Shanghai had already sensed a turnaround. Furthermore, the Ningbo Guild, which had previously sold short over 10,000 piculs due to the sharp price drop in that area and a lack of buyers, today covered the previous short positions in full, further intensifying the upward trend. However, based on actual observations, there is no extreme upward momentum. The recent sharp decline has simply led to a rapid rebound. It is estimated that the raw materials purchased by various factories are sufficient to meet demand for eight to nine months. Consequently, cotton inventories in Shanghai's warehouses are gradually increasing. According to a survey by Jardine Matheson & Co., the inventory of American cotton in Shanghai is over 151,000 bales.

Standard Cotton Continues to Rise by 0.07 Taels: The Standard Cotton market opened higher following the rebound in U.S. cotton prices, with an increase in buyers in the market, creating a tighter situation. Prices for each month rose by 0.06 to 0.07 taels. The afternoon opening was flat, falling by 0.03 to 0.04 taels, and then rising by 0.02 taels in the second and third sessions. Total trading volume for the day was 93,500 piculs. Sales included 7,200 piculs of Gengfeng, 1,600 piculs of Tongyu, 2,100 piculs of Xincheng, 2,300 piculs of Yifeng, and 2,300 piculs of Tongxing. Purchases included 5,800 piculs of Suilong, 7,600 piculs of Yuchang, and 3,000 piculs of Changfeng. The closing prices for Standard Cotton are listed below:

Raw Cotton Mills Should Eliminate Waste: The spot cotton business remains stagnant. Factories are satisfied with imported cotton, so business intentions remain sluggish.

Excessive Rainfall...Traders Buy In: Yesterday, U.S. cotton rose due to excessive rainfall. Traders bought in, and there was a shortage of sellers, resulting in a quiet but firm market. Futures rose by 12 to 14 points, and spot prices rose by 15 points. British cotton futures rose by 2 to 3 points, and spot prices rose by 9 points. Egyptian cotton spot prices rose by 10 points. Silk and Tea: Shanghai Factories Initiate Sales to Europe. British and French Firms Negotiate Large Spot Transactions Yesterday. The Shanghai foreign silk market has been weak and stagnant due to overseas silk sales. Recently, orders for autumn silk from Marseille, Lyon, and other places have increased, and there has been a sudden demand for raw silk. Sin孚, 連納, 達昌 and other firms have received overseas telegrams requesting the purchase of current white factory silk. British firms are also interested, so they have invited various manufacturers to negotiate. The sales volume for upper and middle grade silk is estimated to be over 200 bales. Once negotiations are completed, the transactions can be recorded, and the price of silk is expected to increase by dozens of taels. The market has suddenly become active.

Slight Movement in Keemun Black Tea Sales to England 197

Yesterday, the Shanghai foreign tea market saw Keemun black tea sales. British firms such as Tien Yu, Jin Long, Ewo, and Dodwell began to take action. A total of over 500 chests were negotiated throughout the city. High-grade tea from Qi Nan was offered at 144 taels, while medium- and low-grade tea was sold at 60-70 taels. Market prices were 20-30 taels higher than before. The green tea market remained sluggish. There were no transactions for Wuyuan Tunxi Zhenmei. Only Zhenmei and Xiumei had some sales, and the market situation remained unchanged.

Grains: Rice Market Gradually Loosening

Shanghai South: Yesterday, approximately 20 boats from various guilds arrived, but warehouse inventory remains abundant. Retail sales in urban and rural stores are watching for sunny weather. Moreover, accumulated inventory is gradually increasing, and the price of foreign rice is falling daily, making people feel tired. The fresh Hougeng market saw a slight decrease in price. The Zhongguan甩 declined by 0.2-0.3 taels. The market for Baodao rice remained unchanged among customers. The market for short rice declined by 0.1-0.2 taels. The market for Luxiangjian and Bian Yuan rice saw sporadic movement, with nearly 100 piculs changing hands and prices decreasing slightly.

Shanghai North: Yesterday, approximately 30 rice boats from Changzhou, Wuxi, and Xianzi arrived in the Zhabei rice market. Changzhou Su Baijeng rice was scarce and sales were weak, and the market was gradually declining. Transactions for rice from Kunshan, Jiangyin, and Yixing were extremely light, with prices decreasing by 0.2 taels. Early Baodao rice saw slight demand from tea shops, with an opening price of 0.15 taels less. Bian Yuan rice saw no gain or loss.

3,000 Bags of Wenzhou Rice Newly Arrived 198

Foreign Rice Continues to Fall by 0.15 Taels: Continued Inquiries from Jiangbei in the Interior. Yesterday, the foreign rice and Kejian markets both showed weakness. Because many boats arrived downstream, Tu rice first weakened, and Kejian followed. Yesterday, 3,000 bags of new Wenzhou rice arrived, but no buyer opened a sale. Ke Yuan also had Jiangxi arrivals, but although the quantity was not large, the market was also weak. Yesterday, only 38 bags of Jiangxi Ji Yuan were opened, with a price of 14.4 yuan, about 0.2 yuan less than the price at the beginning of the week.

Foreign rice inventory is very sufficient and continues to arrive recently. Yesterday, it was reported that 5 million bags of Siamese rice were arriving, making people feel weaker and prices decreasing by 0.15 taels. No. 1 Saigon was opened at 300 bags with a price of 11.55 yuan, and Xiao Jiao was opened at 3,200 bags with a price of 10.17 to 10 yuan. The Si Gong rice was handled by the local street, while the Xiao Jiao rice was packaged by Jiangbei's local guilds. The report that 5 million bags of Luo rice were exported and 2 million bags have already arrived refers to the entire Chinese market. Because the Siamese rice stored in Shanghai does not exceed 10,000 bags and the number of bags that have not arrived are also limited, the large amount of imports are to Liangguang and the southern provinces.

Difficulty in Reversing the Flour Market 199

Yesterday, after the flour market opened in the morning, the prices of each month initially stabilized. Because the price of foreign wheat rebounded by about 0.3-0.4 yuan, the opening price was about 0.01 yuan higher than the previous day. However, after the second session, because actual sales were still sluggish and there was no movement, trading was rare, and the market trended dull again. When the afternoon market opened, trading in each month was very rare. Customers' minds were not active. The major factories were still hesitating between selling and not selling. Because there were very few buyers, it was useless to sell, so they were still observing. However, small factories released some sales. In the future, the market must be active in the north before it can improve. As a result, July was unchanged from the previous day, August, September, and October decreased by 0.025 yuan, and November decreased by 0.075 yuan.

Period Wheat is Close to a Distant Drop 200

Yesterday, after the opening of period wheat, the price of foreign wheat rose by 0.3-0.4 yuan and due to the remaining trend from the previous day, people were still in a good mood. The opening price for July was 2.6 yuan, and the opening price for August was 3.6 yuan. However, the situation in the border area was still not good, and the current wheat price was very cheap. The Jiangnei gangs were all paying attention to throwing it out, so they used the current price to throw out the period. There were profits to be made, so it turned flat again. When the afternoon market opened, July seemed to be stable, but the market for August and below was sluggish due to the Jiangnei gangs gradually issuing sales, and the market declined step by step. Looking at the future, it is temporarily considered a distant drop. As a result, July was 0.01 yuan better than the previous day, August and September fell by 0.02 yuan, October fell by 0.05 yuan, and November fell by 0.04 yuan. The market for the current wheat saw an influx of arrivals, and the factory's taste was flat. Yesterday, 300 bags of Qishuyan Gaomai were opened, with a price of 2.92 yuan.

New Shrimp and Dried Squid Arrive, Sales are Weak 201

Ningbo Dried Squid: The new batch of dried squid has arrived in large quantities. According to statistics, the total amount received is over 10,000 piculs. Therefore, the price has continued to decline. The price for first-class goods is 27 taels, high-quality goods are 21 taels, ordinary goods are 20 taels, and lower-quality goods are 18-19 taels. Although the market price has fallen, sales are still very sluggish. Most of the goods that have arrived are sitting in warehouses. The industry wants to sell quickly, but there are no people asking about it. If sales do not increase, there is little hope of a rebound.

Dried Longan (Guìyuán) from North and South is Weak Due to Sluggish Sales 202

Dried Longan (Guìyuán) sales are abnormally weak as the season approaches mold. Although market inventory is not thick, demand is low, prices are falling repeatedly, and there are hopes for a bumper harvest of new Guiyuan from various production areas, so it is difficult to improve market prices. It is reported that recently, the numbers have been continuously opening, and the price has dropped. It is reported that it is seven or eight taels different from the high price.

All Piece Goods (Pǐtóu) Fall, both Domestic and Foreign 203

Piece goods (Pǐtóu) cloth have been falling for days, and customer sales are experiencing a shortage. While foreign cotton markets are falling sharply, and cotton yarn has been shaken by them, piece goods are being greatly affected. The decline recently has been greater than ever before. Coarse cloth of 16 pounds has fallen four to five cents per piece. Ewo's double elephant opened yesterday at only 7 taels, causing the prices of Dasheng and Qingfeng factories to be exceptionally chaotic. 9-pound cloth for Ewo once opened at 3.95 taels, but the market had to be four taels in the afternoon. Fine cloth and fine twill are more vulnerable and have fallen below 7 taels. In fact, the price of yarn has fallen sharply, and the Japanese factory goods are moving again. Most of the customers are waiting and watching, so the supply exceeds the demand. Western goods calling firms have opened for auction as usual, but there are more falls than rises. It is feared that the summer goods will not be sold out. After one look, the goods were still in loss. Blue striped rush cloth is falling, and it is difficult to sell at 1.8 cents. White striped rush cloth is still hard. Rush cloth has also fallen, and Deji Huang Tianbao sold 1.8 cents yesterday. Taisi, Yuan Yuchou, had already started in previous years, but remains unchanged this year.

Comments

Mandarin 204

— Buddha

Our country's authorities are now talking a lot about the issue of resuming diplomatic relations with Russia. They have decided on two principles and two steps, but under the current circumstances, whether Soviet Russia is willing to resume diplomatic relations with our country is also a question.

For example, if I go to a park to pursue a woman, whether the woman is willing to accept my pursuit is also a question. Perhaps she dislikes that I am old, or perhaps she dislikes that I am not handsome. This kind of pursuit is called "one-sided love." Even if she accepts, or if it is only for friendship and she is unwilling to sacrifice her beauty, it is also "lovers are hard to become family members." Now, it is a question whether our country should resume diplomatic relations with Soviet Russia. It is also a question whether Soviet Russia is willing to resume diplomatic relations with us. After resuming diplomatic relations, it is also a question whether Soviet Russia is willing to sacrifice its beauty for us. Firstly, Japan, having heard news of the resumption of diplomatic relations between China and Russia (not necessarily seen in the newspaper), has already planned to restore diplomatic relations between Japan and Russia, and our country has followed suit. Secondly, before Soviet Russia's new five-year plan is successful, it does not seem willing to start a war with Japan. Even if diplomatic relations are resumed, it would be useless.

According to a previous telegram from a Japanese newspaper, "Russia does not seem as eager as before to immediately engage in trade and send envoys, but if China is eager for the Chinese and Russian governments to restore diplomatic relations, their country is also willing to talk." According to this news, it can be seen that Soviet Russia has no sincerity in resuming diplomatic relations with our country. Firstly, it says, "If China is eager," and secondly, it says, "Also willing to talk." Its cold and insincere attitude is already implied. According to yesterday's news from Beijing, the disclosure of the resumption of diplomatic relations too early has caused misunderstandings with the other party, and it is now planned to proceed with another method, which is like Mr. Luo's saying, "One leak will lead to failure," isn't it? This is called "blaming the knife grinder instead of blaming the murderer."

Frosted Glass Photography Lead Plate Making Method 206

— Tang Sicheng

Photographic platemaking is one of the applications of chemistry. Taking negatives is the most important thing. However, the old habits of Chinese people emphasize penmanship and regard retouching as the most important thing. They do not pay attention to chemical effects and platemaking principles. Isn't this abandoning the fundamentals and pursuing the superficial? This is also one of the reasons why platemaking has not progressed. Now, let's try to outline the method of making a lead plate by frosted glass photography on the left.

(1) If you want to make seven colors for a color original, you should first use a color separation filter to take a yellow, red, blue, and black version of each sheet with a color separation dry plate. This kind of technology can be done by those who understand the dry plate, photography, developing, and printing.

Short Measure, Generous Yard, Don't Count the Acre 207

— Benben

"Ah, got opium dross..." A sallow-faced, narrow-shouldered, registered vagrant old man, carrying a woven straw bag with straps on his shoulder, dragging a pair of broken shoes with worn-out heels, listlessly wandered through the alley, chanting the above slogan. When he started calling out, his lips, flapping up and down, revealed his unique trademark: opium dross. Compared to the Misses' lipstick, it seemed even more brightly colored and eye-catching. This was not only his trademark but also, perhaps, the natural machine that demonstrated the sole test of his merchandise. Driven by life and to meet the needs of the lower class of registered vagrants in modern society, he had come to engage in this occupation outside of the 360 traditional trades.

Before long, his slogan prompted someone to call out, "Selling opium dross!" Hearing that business was coming, he immediately ran up to make contact with unsteady steps.

"How much is this bag worth?" A young woman with a sleepy look, wearing embroidered slippers, asked the price.

The old man took a look at the opium dross, then stuffed some into his natural machine to test its potency as part of his inspection process. After finishing the appraisal, he said, "Two hundred coppers."

"No, no, you don't know the goods. Look closely, this is raw opium! Do you think it's bad stuff? I want to sell it for four hundred coppers!"

"Oh dear! Small business, small profit, can't budge that much. Be reasonable, I'll add five coppers,"

"At least three hundred and fifty, not a copper less. I'd rather not sell it," the young woman said firmly.

"First deal of the day, doesn't count. I'll add three more, okay?"

"I said three hundred and fifty, not a copper less. If you don't want it, no problem," the young woman said, picking up the opium dross from the ground and walking away.

"Ah! You rich people can afford raw opium, yet you haggle over two coppers like it's so important. I won't make any profit, fine, fine, fine, three hundred and fifty it is!" Hearing the old man agree to her request, the young woman immediately turned around with a smile, handed the bag of opium dross to the old man, and paid the exact amount. In the end, they completed the transaction.

As the old man walked out of the alley, he thought to himself, "These people really don't understand. If they're so stingy, then how can they afford raw opium that costs thousands of dollars per ounce? Since such expensive raw opium doesn't make them flinch, then why do they haggle over these two coppers like it's life or death? Could it be that two coppers are more valuable than raw opium that costs thousands of dollars per ounce? Ah! This is truly called 'Short measure, generous yard, don't count the acre.'"

Business

The Tailor's Apprentice 208

— Yiping

Agou was twelve years old. All day long, he played riding imaginary horses and rolling copper coins under the oxcart shed with the neighborhood children. Agou's parents were busy with farm work and had no time to discipline their son.

One day, Agou's godmother came to visit his parents. Seeing that Agou was more intelligent and lively than before, she said to him with a smile, "Would you like me to take you to Shanghai to play?" Of course, the child was so happy that he clung to his godmother and wouldn't leave her side. So, the "going to Shanghai to play" was not an empty promise. His godmother's godson ran a clothing store in Shanghai. With the permission of Agou's parents, his godmother recommended him to work as an apprentice in the clothing store.

In the first few days, Agou did nothing but sweep the floor, wipe the tables, and other trivial tasks. In his spare time, he enjoyed looking at the street scenes of Shanghai, which were much more interesting than the rice paddies and oxcart sheds of his village. However, as the weather gradually became hotter, the apprentices had no beds and slept on the floor. Bedbugs disturbed his sleep, and his chubby limbs became covered with red bumps.

Because business was good when making summer clothes, the store hired additional master tailors. Agou was assigned the additional task of cooking porridge in the morning. While the master tailors worked, they instructed him to fan them, which he secretly thought was the best job since coming to the store. Because he would work up a sweat cooking porridge in the morning, and then work up another sweat cooking lunch, with this back and forth with the heat and cold, Agou had become much thinner by the end of the summer.

When the master tailor had his second son, Agou, like a servant, was also responsible for washing diapers. After finishing their meal, the master tailor's wife would go play mahjong, leaving the child in his care. Thus, Agou was busier than anyone else.

In the blink of an eye, Agou had been at the store for almost a year. On a snowy morning, he took a basket to buy groceries (this was another newly added task). After returning, he made tea, washed vegetables... The seasons continued to pass, and Agou's workload only increased.

During the New Year, Agou's mother came from the countryside to see him. She was shocked at how much thinner Agou had become. Agou also cried and wanted to go back home. Fortunately, the master tailor granted him permission to return to his hometown. (That is, the master tailor gave him two yuan for shoes and socks.)

Agou went back to playing imaginary horses with the neighborhood children under the oxcart shed! After working as a tailor's apprentice for a year, he had never held a needle or thread. Therefore, Agou still doesn't understand how a piece of cloth becomes a piece of clothing.

Jiangsu Higher Court Second Branch 209

Criminal Judgments One case of Zhou Kuilin for endangering the Republic of China (Main Text) Zhou Kuilin is sentenced to five years of imprisonment for organizing a group with the aim of endangering the Republic of China. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. The reactionary documents are confiscated. One case of Wang Shunfu and others for using counterfeit currency (Main Text) The original judgment is reversed. Wang Shunfu, who received the counterfeit banknotes and continued to use them after knowing they were counterfeit, is fined one hundred yuan. Shi Zipeng, who received the counterfeit banknotes and incited others to use them after knowing they were counterfeit, is fined one hundred yuan. If the fines are not paid in full, two yuan shall be converted into one day of imprisonment. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the fine at a rate of one day for two yuan. Two counterfeit ten-yuan banknotes of the Bank of China are confiscated. One case of Dai Ronglin and others for abduction (Main Text) The original judgment concerning Dai Ronglin is reversed. Dai Ronglin is sentenced to two years of imprisonment for each of the two crimes of jointly receiving the abducted person with the intention of making a profit. The sentences shall be served consecutively for a total of two years and six months. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. The appeal of Wang Xirong is dismissed.

Civil Judgments One case of Sun Chunsheng for compensation dispute appeal (Main Text) The original judgment is changed. The appeal of the appellee is dismissed. The costs of litigation in the first and second instances shall be borne by the appellee.

Civil Rulings One case of Sheng Zhongfu versus Dacheng Silk Shop Guo Si San for debt dispute application for restoration of original status (Main Text) The application is dismissed. The costs of the application shall be borne by the applicant. One case of Zhang Amao and others for extortion in Shanghai (Main Text) The original judgment is reversed except for the part of Chen Hongsheng's innocence. Zhang Amao, Wang Zhifang, Zhu Asi, and Wang Ali are each sentenced to ten years of imprisonment for joint robbery. Yu Changyou, Ji Aqi, Wang Depu, Li Mengfei, and Zhang Jusheng are each sentenced to seven years of imprisonment for conspiracy to commit robbery. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. Three handguns, twenty-four bullets, and one letter are confiscated. One case of Xie Changhai's appeal for robbery (Main Text) The appeal is dismissed.

Guo Wu Shi versus Guo Zhengxing for assault (Main Text) The private prosecution in this case is dismissed. Laoza Police Station versus Ma Yongfu for theft (Main Text) Ma Yongfu, a habitual offender, is sentenced to three years of imprisonment for theft. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. Zhao Furong versus Ye Shaoqing for embezzlement (Main Text) This case is not accepted. General Patrol Station versus Tang Rixin for receiving stolen goods (Main Text) Tang Rixin, a recidivist for receiving stolen goods, is sentenced to two years of imprisonment. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. Meng Jintao versus Jiang Wanggui for negligent injury (Main Text) Jiang Wanggui is fined two hundred yuan for negligent injury. If the fine is not paid, three yuan shall be converted into one day of imprisonment. Two-year probation. Jiang Wanggui shall compensate Meng Jintao 300 yuan for medical and other expenses. Laoza Police Station versus Li Jiarong for interfering with a family (Main Text) Li Jiarong is sentenced to six months of imprisonment for enticing a woman under the age of twenty with the intention of making a profit. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. Two-year probation. Xinzha Police Station versus Chen Wangshi and others for opium (Main Text) Chen Wangshi is sentenced to six months of imprisonment with a fine of two hundred yuan for the crime of trafficking opium. Gao Ahua is sentenced to one year of imprisonment with a fine of three hundred yuan for providing premises for others to smoke opium with the intention of making a profit. Yuan Zhongxing, Xia Acheng, and Zhang Asan are each sentenced to two months of imprisonment with a fine of fifty yuan for the crime of smoking opium. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be deducted from the term of imprisonment at a rate of two days for one day. If the fines are not paid, two yuan shall be converted into one day of imprisonment. Opium account books, opium soil, opium bubbles, opium ash, opium money, and opium paraphernalia are confiscated. Huang Afu, Shen Baolin, and Xuan Baisheng are found not guilty.

First Instance Civil Judgments Diyi Sassoon versus Li Yutang and others for guarantee and debt (Main Text) The defendant Li Yutang shall repay the plaintiff 3,000 taels of silver, with a statutory late payment interest rate of 5% per annum from the date of the lawsuit to the date of the end of execution. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. Five-sixths of the litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant Li Yutang, with the remaining one-sixth borne by the plaintiff. En Hueck's Clock Factory versus Ying Changxiang Clock and Watch Company Wanxiang Li Bill Certificate Case (Main Text) The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 2,130 Swiss francs with an interest rate of 0.7% per month from November 13th of last year to the end of execution. This judgment shall be subject to provisional enforcement. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. Ye Guisheng versus Tang Zhushi Debt Case (Main Text) The court's judgment on this case made on October 24th, 1931, shall be upheld. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The application costs shall be borne by the defendant. Patridham versus Sun Naizhao and others Loan Case (Main Text) The defendant Sun Naizhao shall repay the plaintiff 200 silver dollars. If he is unable to repay, the defendants Wang Ziyun and Jin Yongsheng shall be jointly and severally liable for repayment. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant Sun Naizhao. Zhang Deyou versus Heng Changchun and others Compensation Case (Main Text) The plaintiff's claims are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. Sun Wuying versus Deng Jinchu Rent Case (Main Text) The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 880 taels of silver. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. Shuntai Manager Ding Xiezhong versus Lao Dashun Grocery Store Owner Gu Daoye Debt Case (Main Text) The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 375.75 silver dollars. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. This case is approved for provisional enforcement. Zhu Deji versus Zhu Ahe Debt Case (Main Text) The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 158.36 silver dollars, of which 100 silver dollars shall be paid with interest at a rate of 1% per month from June 9th, 1931, to the end of execution. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. Gera Xin versus Zhuang Chang and others Debt Case (Main Text) The defendant Zhuang Dechang shall repay the plaintiff 100 silver dollars. This amount shall be repaid in monthly installments of 10 silver dollars until it is paid off. If he is unable to repay, the defendant Zhuang Dekun shall repay on his behalf. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. Tass versus Cubyak, a white Russian, Compensation Case (Main Text) The defendant shall return 225 silver dollars to the plaintiff, and shall compensate the plaintiff 200 silver dollars for losses. The defendant shall return the two hair-waving machines and one rack repaired by the defendant on behalf of the plaintiff. The plaintiff's remaining claims are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. Yao Zichun versus Hu Canghe and others Bill Case (Main Text) The plaintiff's claims are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff. Zhu Guifu versus Gu Wenchao Debt Case (Main Text) The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 550 taels of silver. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. Leng Mosheng versus Du Henggang Loan Case (Main Text) The defendant shall repay the plaintiff 200 silver dollars. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant. Ye Dalong versus Xu Kuibao and others Debt Case (Main Text) The defendant Xu Kuibao shall repay the plaintiff 300 silver dollars, with interest at a rate of 2% per annum from October 1st, 1930, to the date of repayment. If he is unable to repay, the defendant Wan Xuanqing shall be responsible for repayment. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant Xu Kuibao. Jin Wenhua versus Wang Xingchu and others Debt Case (Main Text) The plaintiff's claims are dismissed. The litigation costs shall be borne by the plaintiff. Jiang Hengsheng versus Li Fulai and others Debt Case (Main Text) The defendant Li Fulai shall repay the plaintiff 180 silver dollars. This amount shall be repaid in monthly installments of 9 silver dollars until it is paid off. If he is unable to repay, the defendant Zhang Zi'an shall repay on his behalf. The litigation costs shall be borne by the defendant.

Public Auction Notice For the matter of public auction notice, this court is executing the case of Pu Niansi for tax evasion. The assets owned by the defendant have been seized and appraised. The auction date is set for June 21st. The court will send a clerk to direct the execution officer to conduct the auction. All residents who wish to purchase these assets should report to the court's execution officer's office to be led to the location to view the assets and then follow the schedule to bid. If there are two or more bidders, the person with the highest bid will be the purchaser. The full price of silver will be paid on the spot, and the auctioned assets will be given to the purchaser for collection. All residents are hereby notified. This is a public announcement. Details are as follows: (1) Subject of the auction: movable property (list attached separately); (2) Location of the property: Nos. 619 and 620 Zhaofeng Road, Hongkou; (3) Minimum price: 364.60 silver dollars; (4) Place to view the records: the office of the court's execution officer; (5) Execution clerk: Zhu Guangzhao; Execution officers: Liu Yulin and Xu Yingjie. (June 16th)

Shanghai Second Special District Local Court 211

Criminal Judgment: Fang Ganchen is sentenced to one year of imprisonment and fined 500 yuan for the crime of manufacturing opium substitutes. The case of private prosecutor Zhang Lushi suing Hu Jiazhen for suspected murder is not accepted. The case of private prosecutor Su Meimei suing Wang Jinhe for obstruction is not accepted.

Criminal Instruction: Regarding He Huiguang's request to issue a subpoena for evidence, the court acknowledges the petition and will schedule a hearing to review the matter. Regarding Yu Zaishan (also known as Zhan Shan)'s request to suspend detention, the court acknowledges the petition and orders the petitioner to pay a bail of 300 yuan to be granted suspension of detention.

Civil Instruction: Regarding She Hu'er Shi's divorce from Xia Erdi Wei Luo Ke, the court acknowledges the petition and records the matter. Regarding Commercial Printing House Han Jie's request to close the case, the court acknowledges the petition and grants the closure. Regarding Chongde Company Kong Tingnan's request to close the case and receive funds, the court acknowledges the petition. Since the debtor has paid off the case funds, the request for closure should be granted. All filed funds and the sealing fee previously paid by the petitioner should be collected at the court at 9:00 AM on the 17th of this month. Regarding Xinkang Company Lü Xuanqing's request to close the case and be exempted from execution, the court acknowledges the petition and grants the closure. Regarding Dong Jinqing's request to receive funds, the court acknowledges the petition. This case previously involved the sealing of debtor Jiang Runzhi's movable property. Subsequently, Yu Likun sued the debtor for rent arrears, and the cases were combined for execution, appraisal, and auction. The requested matter should be scheduled for a hearing to clarify and allocate proportionally. The petitioner should be notified. Regarding Gu Shan Jin's request for execution, the court acknowledges the petition. This case was previously scheduled for a hearing on May 26th for execution. The petitioner did not appear on the scheduled date. The requested matter should be scheduled for another hearing. The petitioner should comply with the deadline to attend the hearing. The petitioner should be notified. Regarding Shen Fugen's request to file a record for relocating sealed property and terminating the lease, the court acknowledges the petition. This court sealed Wei Mao Gou's property due to a case that was resolved through reconciliation, and officials were instructed to lift the seal and issue it to Wei Mao Gou for collection. The termination of the lease requires a lawsuit and cannot be resolved by filing a record. The petitioner should be notified. Regarding Jia Fuyu's request to continue enforcement, the court acknowledges the petition. This case was previously heard on February 15th of this year. The debtor stated in court that, in addition to 92 yuan to be repaid in two installments (which has already been collected), the remaining principal, interest, and litigation costs totaled 270 yuan, to be repaid in four installments starting in August of this year. The petitioner indicated agreement on record. The outstanding amount has not yet become due. If the debtor is unable to fulfill the obligation at the due date, the petitioner can request enforcement again. Regarding Wang Yongmei's request to collect evidence, the court acknowledges the petition and instructs the petitioner to come to the court at 2:00 PM on the 20th of this month to collect the evidence. Regarding Shao Laisheng and Wang Shouquan's request to add a defendant for rent arrears, the court acknowledges the petition. The case has been adjudicated, and the request cannot be approved. The petitioner should file a separate case for mediation. Regarding Fu Yaodong's request to suspend sealing, the court acknowledges the petition. The petitioner should pay Tai Li Company 150 taels of rent, 7 yuan and 2 jiao in litigation costs, and 1 yuan, 3 jiao, and 5 fen in enforcement fees to the court before the 20th of this month. Otherwise, the sealing will proceed.
